<td colspan="4" style="text-align:center;border-bottom:1px solid #aaa;line-height:1.5em;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lebanese_insurgency.svg"><img alt="Lebanese insurgency.svg" data-file-height="1142" data-file-width="992" height="345" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Lebanese_insurgency.svg/300px-Lebanese_insurgency.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Lebanese_insurgency.svg/450px-Lebanese_insurgency.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Lebanese_insurgency.svg/600px-Lebanese_insurgency.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a><br/>
<div style="text-align: left;">Military situation in Lebanon on 6 June 2016<br/>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ffa067; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Lebanon" title="Politics of Lebanon">Lebanese Government</a></div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #3e79ff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Controlled by <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a></div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #b3b2ae; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant</a> (ISIL)</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #fff7fd; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Controlled by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Nusra_Front" title="Al-Nusra Front">Al-Nusra Front</a> and other Sunni militants</div>
(For a more detailed map, see <a href="/wiki/Template:Lebanese_insurgency_detailed_map" title="Template:Lebanese insurgency detailed map">Map of the Lebanese insurgency</a>)</div>
</td>

<ul>

<div aria-labelledby="Civil_conflicts_in_Lebanon" class="navbox" role="navigation" style="margin:0;float:right;clear:right;width:315px;margin-bottom:0.5em;margin-left:1em;;padding:3px">
<table class="nowraplinks collapsible autocollapse navbox-inner" style="border-spacing:0;background:transparent;color:inherit">
<tr>
<th class="navbox-title" colspan="2" scope="col" style="background-color:#B0C4DE;">
<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
<ul>
<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Campaignbox_Lebanon_conflicts" title="Template:Campaignbox Lebanon conflicts"><abbr style=";background-color:#B0C4DE;;background:none transparent;border:none;" title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Campaignbox_Lebanon_conflicts" title="Template talk:Campaignbox Lebanon conflicts"><abbr style=";background-color:#B0C4DE;;background:none transparent;border:none;" title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Campaignbox_Lebanon_conflicts&amp;action=edit"><abbr style=";background-color:#B0C4DE;;background:none transparent;border:none;" title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>
</ul>
</div>
<div id="Civil_conflicts_in_Lebanon" style="font-size:114%"><span style="line-height:1.6em">Civil conflicts in <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a></span></div>
</th>
</tr>
<tr style="height:2px">
<td colspan="2"></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" colspan="2" style="width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/1958_Lebanon_crisis" title="1958 Lebanon crisis">1958 Lebanon crisis</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Civil_War" title="Lebanese Civil War">Lebanese Civil War</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bab_al-Tabbaneh%E2%80%93Jabal_Mohsen_conflict" title="Bab al-Tabbaneh–Jabal Mohsen conflict">Bab al-Tabbaneh–Jabal Mohsen</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dinnieh_fighting" title="Dinnieh fighting">Dinnieh fighting</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cedar_Revolution" title="Cedar Revolution">Cedar Revolution</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/2007_Lebanon_conflict" title="2007 Lebanon conflict">2007 Lebanon conflict</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/2008_conflict_in_Lebanon" title="2008 conflict in Lebanon">2008 conflict in Lebanon</a></li>
<li><strong class="selflink">Syrian Civil War spillover in Lebanon</strong></li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
</div>
<p>Fighting from the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Civil_War" title="Syrian Civil War">Syrian Civil War</a> has <a href="/wiki/Spillover_of_the_Syrian_Civil_War" title="Spillover of the Syrian Civil War">spilled over</a> into <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a> as opponents and supporters of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syrian_rebels" title="Syrian rebels">Syrian rebels</a> have travelled to Lebanon to fight and attack each other on Lebanese soil. The Syrian conflict has been described as having stoked a "resurgence of sectarian violence in Lebanon",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-holmes_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-holmes-50">[50]</a></sup> with many of Lebanon's <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam_in_Lebanon" title="Sunni Islam in Lebanon">Sunni</a> Muslims supporting the rebels in Syria, while many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shi%27a_Islam_in_Lebanon" title="Shi'a Islam in Lebanon">Shi'ites</a> have supported Assad, whose <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alawites_in_Lebanon" title="Alawites in Lebanon">Alawite</a> minority is usually described as an offshoot of Shi'a Islam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bassam_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-bassam-51">[51]</a></sup> Killings, unrest, and kidnappings of foreign citizens across <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a> have resulted.</p>
<p>In mid-2011, seven people were killed and 59 wounded in a fight between gunmen in Tripoli. In May 2012, the conflict spread to Beirut, and later to south and east Lebanon, while the <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Armed_Forces" title="Lebanese Armed Forces">Lebanese Armed Forces</a> deployed in north Lebanon and Beirut. As of January 2016 there have been more than 800 fatalities and almost 3,000 injuries. Among Lebanon's political blocs the anti-Syrian <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi</a>-backed <a href="/wiki/March_14_Alliance" title="March 14 Alliance">March 14 Alliance</a> supports the Syrian rebels, and the <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iranian</a>-backed pro-Syrian <a href="/wiki/March_8_Alliance" title="March 8 Alliance">March 8 Alliance</a> supports the Syrian government.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lebanese_army_in_Tripoli.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="471" data-file-width="852" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Lebanese_army_in_Tripoli.PNG/220px-Lebanese_army_in_Tripoli.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Lebanese_army_in_Tripoli.PNG/330px-Lebanese_army_in_Tripoli.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Lebanese_army_in_Tripoli.PNG/440px-Lebanese_army_in_Tripoli.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lebanese_army_in_Tripoli.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Lebanese army in <a href="/wiki/Tripoli,_Lebanon" title="Tripoli, Lebanon">Tripoli</a> after sectarian clashes, in 2012.</div>

<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lebanese_Sectarian_Clashes_Spark_Syria_Spillover_Fears.ogv" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
2012 <a href="/wiki/Voice_of_America" title="Voice of America">VOA</a> report about the context of the conflict</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since the <a href="/wiki/Cedar_Revolution" title="Cedar Revolution">Cedar Revolution</a> in 2005 and the withdrawal of the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_occupation_of_Lebanon" title="Syrian occupation of Lebanon">occupying Syrian forces</a> from the country, the Lebanese political spectrum has been divided between the anti-Syrian government March 14 alliance and the pro-Syrian government March 8 alliance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> The March 14 alliance, led by the mainly <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam_in_Lebanon" title="Sunni Islam in Lebanon">Sunni</a> Muslim <a href="/wiki/Future_Movement" title="Future Movement">Future Movement</a>, which is allied with the <a href="/wiki/Maronite_Christianity_in_Lebanon" title="Maronite Christianity in Lebanon">Maronite Christian</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lebanese_Forces_Party" title="Lebanese Forces Party">Lebanese Forces Party</a>, has called for Lebanese aid to the <a href="/wiki/Free_Syrian_Army" title="Free Syrian Army">Free Syrian Army</a> and taking a stronger stance against the Syrian government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>This has been rejected by the ruling March 8 alliance, which includes the Shia <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a> and allies such as the Maronite <a href="/wiki/Free_Patriotic_Movement" title="Free Patriotic Movement">Free Patriotic Movement</a>, among others. In August, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jerusalem_Post" title="The Jerusalem Post">The Jerusalem Post</a></i> reported that protesters, enraged at Hezbollah's support for Syria's government, burned Hezbollah flags and images of its leader <a href="/wiki/Hassan_Nasrallah" title="Hassan Nasrallah">Hassan Nasrallah</a> in several places in Syria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Pro-government protestors countered the actions by carrying posters of Nasrallah.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Hezbollah states they support a process of reforms in Syria and that they are also against U.S. plots to destabilize and interfere in Syria,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> amid comments by U.S. Secretary of State Hillary Clinton that it should be "abundantly clear to those who support Assad [the] 'regime' [that] its days are numbered."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> It was reported that, "sales of black market weapons in Lebanon have skyrocketed in recent weeks due to demand in Syria."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> In June 2011, clashes in the Lebanese city of Tripoli between members of the Alawite minority, loyal to Syrian President <a href="/wiki/Bashar_al-Assad" title="Bashar al-Assad">Bashar al-Assad</a>, and members of the Sunni majority left seven people dead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aljazeera1_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-aljazeera1-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>Future Movement MP <a href="/wiki/Okab_Sakr" title="Okab Sakr">Okab Sakr</a> was long suspected to be involved in aiding the insurgents in the Syrian civil war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> At first he denied his involvement, but admitted it when <i><a href="/wiki/Al_Akhbar_(Lebanon)" title="Al Akhbar (Lebanon)">Al Akhbar</a></i> published audio tapes of him making arms deals with Syrian insurgents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Sakr later claimed the tapes were edited, and that he only provided Syrians with milk and blankets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>Sunni extremists from Tripoli have been flocking to Syria to join the terrorist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Nusra_Front" title="Al-Nusra Front">Al-Nusra Front</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Hezbollah fighters have been deployed to protect border towns inhabited by Lebanese Shias from the rebels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lebanese_Army" title="Lebanese Army">Lebanese Army</a> has attempted to disassociate itself from the conflict in Syria, and to prevent clashes within Lebanon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Timeline">Timeline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Syrian_Civil_War_spillover_in_Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Timeline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_violent_events_relating_to_the_Syrian_Civil_War_spillover_in_Lebanon_(2011%E2%80%9314)" title="Timeline of violent events relating to the Syrian Civil War spillover in Lebanon (2011–14)">Timeline of violent events relating to the Syrian Civil War spillover in Lebanon (2011–14)</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timeline_of_violent_events_relating_to_the_Syrian_Civil_War_spillover_in_Lebanon_(2014%E2%80%94Present)" title="Timeline of violent events relating to the Syrian Civil War spillover in Lebanon (2014—Present)">Timeline of violent events relating to the Syrian Civil War spillover in Lebanon (2014—Present)</a></div>
<p>From the inception of the violence that began in Syria as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">Arab Spring</a>, the Syrian Civil War has produced and inspired a great deal of strife and unrest among armed factions. Prior to the Battle of Arsal in August 2014, the Lebanese Army has tried to keep out of it and the violence has been mostly between various factions within the country and overt Syrian involvement has been limited to airstrikes and occasional accidental incursions.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_battles_2014.E2.80.9315">Major battles 2014–15</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Syrian_Civil_War_spillover_in_Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Major battles 2014–15">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Arsal_(2014)" title="Battle of Arsal (2014)">Battle of Arsal (2014)</a></div>
<p>In June 2014, a joint brigade of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-Nusra_Front" title="Al-Nusra Front">Al-Nusra Front</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISIL" title="ISIL">ISIL</a> troops invaded and briefly held the town of Arsal, leading to a major battle and hostage taking. It has long been expected that another major push would take place in Lebanon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>A year later, in June 2015, <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Hassan_Nasrallah" title="Hassan Nasrallah">Hassan Nasrallah</a> claimed that ISIL and Nusra had seized territory within Lebanon and that major fighting was going on between them and Hezbollah, as well as each other <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recapture_of_territories">Recapture of territories</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Syrian_Civil_War_spillover_in_Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Recapture of territories">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>By 22 June 2016, 95% of the territory once controlled by militants had been recaptured by Lebanese army and their allies, with only 50 km<sup>2</sup> left under their control. Daily clashes were ongoing mainly near the town of <a href="/wiki/Arsal" title="Arsal">Arsal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> On 22 September, ISIL emir Imad Yassin was arrested from <a href="/wiki/Ain_al-Hilweh" title="Ain al-Hilweh">Ain al-Hilweh</a> refugee camp.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yassin_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-Yassin-48">[48]</a></sup> Clashes erupted between ISIL and Nusra Front in Arsal Barrens on 26 October after ISIL tried to infiltrate towards the Hamid valley.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> On 28 October, the Lebanese Army carried out a raid against ISIL in the Wadi Zarzour area of Jaroud 'Arsal, killing a number of militants and destroying a militant hideout.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> An ISIL commander Ahmad Youssef Amoun was arrested along with 10 other militants on 24 November after a military operation by the Lebanese Army on a center of the group near Arsal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Deaths_and_injuries">Deaths and injuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Syrian_Civil_War_spillover_in_Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Deaths and injuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Casualties_of_the_Syrian_Civil_War_spillover_in_Lebanon" title="Casualties of the Syrian Civil War spillover in Lebanon">Casualties of the Syrian Civil War spillover in Lebanon</a></div>
<p>In the unrest of June 2011, at least 7 deaths were reported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aljazeera1_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-aljazeera1-60">[60]</a></sup> A further 2-3 deaths occurred during the incidents of February 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>Between May 2012 and December 2015, violent political incidents had resulted in at least 789 fatalities and more than 2,700 injuries, mostly during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bab_al_Tabbaneh-Jabal_Mohsen_clashes" title="Bab al Tabbaneh-Jabal Mohsen clashes">Bab al Tabbaneh-Jabal Mohsen clashes</a> in Tripoli. In August 2014, starting with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Arsal" title="Battle of Arsal">battle of Arsal</a> between the Lebanese Army and Sunni militants at the beginning of the month and intense fighting that included both the Syrian and Lebanese armies in and near Arsal and the Bekaa Valley at the end of the month, the fighting had reached a new and different phase. The August casualties nearly equaled half the number of the previous two years put together. 12 November 2015, <a href="/wiki/2015_Beirut_bombings" title="2015 Beirut bombings">bombings in Beirut</a> killed 43 people in the deadliest event of 2015 for this conflict.</p>
<p>The Lebanese Army stated that by June 2016, about 500 ISIL and Nusra militants had been killed and 700 captured in the border area of Lebanon and Syria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions">Reactions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Syrian_Civil_War_spillover_in_Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Reactions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Domestic_political_reactions">Domestic political reactions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Syrian_Civil_War_spillover_in_Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Domestic political reactions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>22 May 2012, Hezbollah deputy leader Sheikh <a href="/wiki/Naim_Qassem" title="Naim Qassem">Naim Qassem</a> condoled Sunni Grand Mufti <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Rashid_Qabbani" title="Mohammed Rashid Qabbani">Mohammed Rashid Qabbani</a> over the killings, and relayed the condolences of <a href="/wiki/Hassan_Nasrallah" title="Hassan Nasrallah">Hassan Nasrallah</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> The same day, Shadi Mawlawi, the Islamist whose arrest sparked the clashes in Tripoli, was released from custody, but Islamist protesters did not stop their sit-in protests, since they wanted 123 other Islamists freed as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> The Future Movement called for Mikati to immediately resign, claiming his cabinet had shown incapability to maintain the country’s security.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Forces" title="Lebanese Forces">Lebanese Forces</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Samir_Geagea" title="Samir Geagea">Samir Geagea</a> accused Hezbollah of training and arming groups in Tripoli.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yalibnan1_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-yalibnan1-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2012, Prime Minister Najib Miqati, a native of Tripoli, issued a statement saying that "efforts to drag Lebanon more and more into the conflict in Syria when what is required is for leaders to cooperate...to protect Lebanon from the danger" and urged the <a href="/wiki/International_community" title="International community">international community</a> to help prevent Lebanon from being another theater in the Syrian civil war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23AugustABCBlog_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-23AugustABCBlog-81">[81]</a></sup> He added: "The cabinet work is not a priority compared to what the country is witnessing when it comes to exposure to the Syrian crisis and attempts to transfer it to Lebanon. The country is in great danger."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/An-Nahar" title="An-Nahar">An Nahar</a></i> cited unnamed "western diplomatic sources" as stating that these incidents were the beginning of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salafist" title="Salafist">Salafist</a> revolution aimed at arming the uprising in Syria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Salafists in Lebanon have often voiced their support for the uprising in Syria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> The March 14 alliance also accused the Syrian government of trying to drag Lebanon into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syrian_civil_war" title="Syrian civil war">its crisis</a>. The Future Movement's former MP <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mustafa_Alloush&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mustafa Alloush (page does not exist)">Mustafa Alloush</a> said after regular weekly meeting: "It is actually an attempt to make of Tripoli a zone of terrorism. It also aims at striking Lebanon's northern area which has welcomed and helped out the Syrian displaced."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-al-akhbar1_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-al-akhbar1-85">[85]</a></sup> Calls by <a href="/wiki/Rifaat_Eid" title="Rifaat Eid">Rifaat Eid</a>, the head of the Arab Democratic Party, for a return of the Syrian army to Tripoli to impose security in the city were rejected by Prime Minister Najib Mikati.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Syrian Civil War and its domestic impact have furthered the polarisation of Lebanese politics. The <a href="/wiki/March_14_Alliance" title="March 14 Alliance">March 14 Alliance</a>, dominated by Christian- and Sunni-based parties, is broadly sympathetic to the Syrian opposition to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bashar_Al-Assad" title="Bashar Al-Assad">Bashar Al-Assad</a>. In August, youth members of 14 March parties including Kataeb, Lebanese Forces, National Liberal Party, Future Movement and Islamic Group held a rally to demand the expulsion of the Syrian Ambassador.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> 8 March parties generally supported the continuation of the Assad government, but analysts believe some groups within the coalition may seek new alliances if the Assad government falls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> More moderate members of the coalition in government have begun distancing themselves from the Assad government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>Previously allied with Assad, the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Socialist_Party" title="Progressive Socialist Party">Progressive Socialist Party</a> of <a href="/wiki/Walid_Jumblatt" title="Walid Jumblatt">Walid Jumblatt</a> have taken an anti-Assad stance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 13 February 2013, more than 182,938 Syrian refugees are in Lebanon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> As the number of Syrian refugees increases, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lebanese_Forces_Party" title="Lebanese Forces Party">Lebanese Forces Party</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kataeb_Party" title="Kataeb Party">Kataeb Party</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Free_Patriotic_Movement" title="Free Patriotic Movement">Free Patriotic Movement</a> fear the country’s sectarian based political system is being undermined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> Other parties, such as the mostly Shia <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lebanese_Option_Gathering" title="Lebanese Option Gathering">Lebanese Option Gathering</a> and the mostly Sunni <a href="/wiki/Najjadeh_Party" title="Najjadeh Party">Najjadeh Party</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> have also taken stances close to 14 March, including calling cancellation of agreements between the two countries.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International">International</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Syrian_Civil_War_spillover_in_Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: International">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Flag_of_the_United_Nations.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Nations.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Flag_of_the_United_Nations.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Nations.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Flag_of_the_United_Nations.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_United_Nations.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">UN</a>: On 21 May 2012, Secretary-General <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a> appealed for calm after the clashes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> On 22 August 2012, Under-Secretary-General for Political Affairs <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_D._Feltman" title="Jeffrey D. Feltman">Jeffrey Feltman</a>, in a meeting of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Security_Council" title="Security Council">Security Council</a>, described the situation as "precarious" and warned that a deteriorating situation in Syria could destabilise Lebanon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCAugust23_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBCAugust23-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>: On 23 May 2012, Foreign Minister <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sergei_Lavrov" title="Sergei Lavrov">Sergei Lavrov</a> said there was a real threat of conflict spilling over from Syria and that it could have a very bad ending.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="750" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Saudi_Arabia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>: On 23 May 2012, <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="Abdullah of Saudi Arabia">King Abdullah</a> wrote to Lebanese President <a href="/wiki/Michel_Suleiman" title="Michel Suleiman">Michel Suleiman</a> expressing concern over the recent violence in Tripoli, especially the sectarian nature of the violence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>: On 25 May 2012, Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> called for restraint and said the U.S. was concerned the unrest in Syria would contribute instability in Lebanon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> In May, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Ambassador_to_Lebanon" title="United States Ambassador to Lebanon">Ambassador</a> <a href="/wiki/Maura_Connelly" title="Maura Connelly">Maura Connelly</a> met with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Lebanon" title="Prime Minister of Lebanon">Lebanese Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Najib_Mikati" title="Najib Mikati">Najib Mikati</a> to express her concern with the security situation in Tripoli and commended the government's efforts to defuse the situation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
